. **Custom type lookup** — First checks if a `DefinedTypeMapFunc` is registered (for user-defined database types like PostgreEnum).
. **Named type lookup** — Checks the dialect's internal type registry (e.g., `"vector"` → `PgType.VECTOR`).
. **Array detection** — If the type name contains `[` (e.g., `"integer[]"`), it resolves the element type then wraps it via `arrayTypeOfThis()`.
. **Fallback** — If no match is found, returns the `defaultType` (the `MappingType.map()` result).

[source,java]
----
// Simplified resolution logic in TypeMappingHandlerSupport
final MappingType handleDefinedType(final String typeName, final MappingType defaultType) {
    // 1. Try user-defined type function
    MappingType type = func.apply(typeName, serverMeta, typeMap);
    if (type != null) return type;

    // 2. Check if it's an array type (e.g., "integer[]")
    final int index = typeName.indexOf('[');
    if (index < 0) {
        type = this.typeMap.getOrDefault(typeName, defaultType);
    } else {
        type = this.typeMap.get(typeName.substring(0, index));  // element type
        if (type != null) {
            type = ((MappingType.SqlArray) type.arrayTypeOfThis()).unlimited();
        } else {
            type = defaultType;
        }
    }
    return type;
}
----

This design means the `MappingType` hierarchy is database-agnostic — each `MappingType` declares its target `DataType` per-dialect in `map()`, and `TypeMappingHandler` provides the final resolution for custom/composite/array types.
In most cases, developers interact only with the `@Mapping` annotation; the handler chain operates transparently behind the scenes.

=== Custom MappingType — Extending the Type System

When the built-in mapping types don't fit your domain, Army provides two abstract base classes for creating custom types.

==== Step 1: Choose the Right Base Class

[cols="2,5,3",options="header"]
|===
| Scenario | Base Class | Example

| Non-array Java type
| Extend `io.army.mapping.UserMappingType`
| A custom `Currency` type mapped to `NUMERIC(10,2)`

| Array Java type
| Extend `io.army.mapping.UserArrayType`
| A custom `IntRange[]` type mapped to PostgreSQL `INT4RANGE[]`
|===

`UserMappingType` extends `AbstractMappingType`, which already provides `beforeBind()` / `afterGet()` defaults (pass-through to `String`).
`UserArrayType` extends `UserMappingType` and additionally implements `ArrayMappingType`.

==== Step 2: Implement the Corresponding `Sql*` Marker Interface

Every mapping type should declare what *kind* of SQL value it represents by implementing one of `MappingType`'s inner marker interfaces.
The Army framework uses these markers for validation and type compatibility checks.

[NOTE]
====
The `map()`, `beforeBind()`, and `afterGet()` methods work regardless of whether you implement a `Sql*` marker — the mapping will execute correctly in basic read/write scenarios.

The problem arises when Army needs to know the *semantic category* of your type.
For example:

* Generating DDL — Army must decide `INT` vs `VARCHAR` vs `TIMESTAMP` column type.
Without a marker, it cannot infer the SQL type family.
* Type compatibility checks — when comparing two columns or assigning a parameter, Army verifies that both sides are in the same type family (e.g., both are `SqlNumber`).
* Array element inference — when creating an array type automatically, Army uses the marker to determine the element SQL type.

In short: your type *will* work without a marker, but it may fail in DDL generation or type-checking scenarios.
Implementing the correct `Sql*` interface is strongly recommended.
====

Common marker interfaces:

[cols="2,3,4",options="header"]
|===
| Category | Interface | When to Use

| Number
| `MappingType.SqlInteger`
| Maps to `INT`. Your type handles integer values.

| Number
| `MappingType.SqlDecimal`
| Maps to `NUMERIC`. Your type handles decimal values.

| String
| `MappingType.SqlText`
| Maps to `TEXT`. Your type handles long unbounded strings.

| String
| `MappingType.SqlString`
| Maps to `VARCHAR`. Your type handles short bounded strings.

| Binary
| `MappingType.SqlBlob`
| Maps to `BYTEA` / `BLOB`. Your type handles binary data.

| JSON
| `MappingType.SqlJson`
| Maps to `JSON`. Your type stores JSON documents.

| Extension
| `MappingType.SqlVector`
| Maps to pgvector `VECTOR` type. Combine with `MappingType.SqlExtension` to auto-create the extension.

| Time
| `MappingType.SqlLocalDateTime`
| Maps to `TIMESTAMP`. Your type handles date-time values.
|===

[TIP]
====
The full list of marker interfaces is in `io.army.mapping.MappingType`:

* **Boolean** — `SqlBoolean`
* **Numeric** — `SqlInteger`, `SqlFloat`, `SqlDecimal`
* **String** — `SqlString`, `SqlText`
* **Binary** — `SqlBinary`, `SqlBlob`, `SqlBit`
* **JSON** — `SqlJson`, `SqlJsonb`
* **Time** — `SqlLocalDate`, `SqlLocalTime`, `SqlLocalDateTime`, `SqlOffsetDateTime`, `SqlDuration`
* **Extension** — `SqlVector`, `SqlExtension`

Pick the one that most closely describes your target SQL type — each has a single unambiguous semantic meaning.
====

==== Step 3: Follow the Implementation Pattern

All built-in mapping types follow a consistent pattern.
Your custom type must adhere to it for framework compatibility:

[source,java]
----
/// Custom mapping: maps a Java `Currency` record to PostgreSQL `NUMERIC(10,2)`.
public final class CurrencyType extends UserMappingType   // io.army.mapping.UserMappingType
        implements MappingType.SqlDecimal {

    // 1. Static factory method — required for @Mapping resolution
    public static CurrencyType from(final Class<?> javaType) {
        if (javaType != Currency.class) {
            throw errorJavaType(CurrencyType.class, javaType);
        }
        return INSTANCE;
    }

    public static final CurrencyType INSTANCE = new CurrencyType();

    // 2. Constructor must be non-public (private or package-private)
    private CurrencyType() {
    }

    // 3. Declare the Java type this mapping handles
    @Override
    public Class<?> javaType() {
        return Currency.class;
    }

    // 4. Map to the concrete SQL DataType per database
    @Override
    public DataType map(final ServerMeta meta) {
        final DataType dataType;
        switch (meta.serverDatabase()) {
            case PostgreSQL:
                dataType = PgType.NUMERIC;
                break;
            case MySQL:
                dataType = MySQLType.DECIMAL;
                break;
            default:
                throw mapError(this, meta);
        }
        return dataType;
    }

    // 5. Serialize Java value → SQL parameter
    @Override
    public BigDecimal beforeBind(DataType dataType, MappingEnv env, Object source) {
        if (!(source instanceof Currency c)) {
            throw paramError(this, dataType, source, null);
        }
        return c.value();
    }

    // 6. Deserialize database value → Java object
    @Override
    public Currency afterGet(DataType dataType, MappingEnv env, Object source) {
        final Currency value;
        if (source instanceof Currency c) {
            value = c;
        } else if (source instanceof BigDecimal bd) {
            value = new Currency(bd);
        } else if (source instanceof String s) {
            value = new Currency(new BigDecimal(s));
        } else {
            throw dataAccessError(this, dataType, source, null);
        }
        return value;
    }

    // 7. Required: override hashCode/equals for singleton types
    @Override
    public int hashCode() {
        return System.identityHashCode(this);
    }

    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object obj) {
        return obj instanceof CurrencyType;
    }
}
----

[IMPORTANT]
====
The `from(Class)` static factory method is how `_MappingFactory.doMap` reflectively creates your MappingType.
Without it, the framework cannot instantiate your type.
The constructor must be non-public — all built-in types use `private` constructors and expose a singleton `INSTANCE`.
====

==== Array Type Example

For array types, extend `UserArrayType` and implement `MappingType.SqlArray`:

[source,java]
----
/// Custom mapping: maps `Currency[]` to PostgreSQL `NUMERIC[]`.
public final class CurrencyArrayType extends UserArrayType
        implements MappingType.SqlArray {

    public static CurrencyArrayType from(final Class<?> javaType) {
        final CurrencyArrayType instance;
        if (javaType == Currency[].class) {
            instance = LINEAR;
        } else if (javaType == Object.class) {
            instance = UNLIMITED;
        } else if (!javaType.isArray()) {
            throw errorJavaType(CurrencyArrayType.class, javaType);
        } else if (ArrayUtils.underlyingComponent(javaType) == Currency.class) {
            instance = new CurrencyArrayType(javaType);
        } else {
            throw errorJavaType(CurrencyArrayType.class, javaType);
        }
        return instance;
    }

    /// Used for default array parsing when the database returns an array
    /// of unknown dimensions. Typically consumed by {@code io.army.dialect.TypeMappingHandler}
    /// implementations.
    public static final CurrencyArrayType UNLIMITED = new CurrencyArrayType(Object.class);

    public static final CurrencyArrayType LINEAR = new CurrencyArrayType(Currency[].class);

    private final Class<?> javaType;

    /// private constructor
    private CurrencyArrayType(Class<?> javaType) {
        this.javaType = javaType;
    }

    @Override
    public final Class<?> javaType() {
        return this.javaType;
    }

    @Override
    public final Class<?> underlyingJavaType() {
        return Currency.class;
    }

    @Override
    public final DataType map(final ServerMeta meta) {
        final DataType dataType;
        switch (meta.serverDatabase()) {
            case PostgreSQL:
                dataType = PgType.NUMERIC_ARRAY;
                break;
            default:
                throw mapError(this, meta);
        }
        return dataType;
    }

    @Override
    public final MappingType elementType() {
        final MappingType instance;
        final Class<?> javaType = this.javaType;
        if (javaType == Object.class) { // unlimited dimension array
            instance = this;
        } else if (javaType == Currency[].class) {
            instance = CurrencyType.INSTANCE;
        } else {
            instance = from(javaType.getComponentType());
        }
        return instance;
    }

    @Override
    public MappingType arrayTypeOfThis() throws CriteriaException {
        final Class<?> javaType = this.javaType;
        if (javaType == Object.class) { // unlimited dimension array
            return this;
        }
        return from(ArrayUtils.arrayClassOf(javaType));
    }

    // beforeBind / afterGet omitted for brevity — see built-in array types for reference

    @Override
    public int hashCode() {
        return this.javaType.hashCode();
    }

    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object obj) {
        final boolean match;
        if (obj == this) {
            match = true;
        } else if (obj instanceof CurrencyArrayType o) {
            match = o.javaType == this.javaType;
        } else {
            match = false;
        }
        return match;
    }
}
----

[TIP]
====
For array types, the element type is obtained from the field's component type via reflection — you do NOT need `@Mapping(elements = ...)`.
The `elements` attribute is only for generic collections (`List<Foo>`, `Set<Bar>`) where type erasure loses the element type.
====

==== Quick Checklist

Before writing your custom type, verify:

- [ ] Non-array type → extends `UserMappingType`; Array type → extends `UserArrayType`
- [ ] Implements the correct `Sql*` marker interface (e.g., `SqlDecimal`, `SqlVector`)
- [ ] Provides a `public static ... from(Class)` factory method
- [ ] Constructor is `private` (or package-private)
- [ ] Overrides `javaType()`, `map()`, `beforeBind()`, `afterGet()`
- [ ] Overrides `hashCode()` and `equals(Object)`
- [ ] For array types, also overrides `underlyingJavaType()`, `elementType()`, and `arrayTypeOfThis()`
- [ ] (Optional) If the type needs a PostgreSQL extension, implements `MappingType.SqlExtension`

=== Full Mapping Chain Summary

[cols="2,5,4",options="header"]
|===
| Stage | What Happens | Example

| 1. **Annotation Processing**
| Army reads `@Mapping` (or infers default) to determine `MappingType`
| `@Mapping("io.army.mapping.optional.VectorType")` → `VectorType`

| 2. **Dialect Resolution**
| `MappingType.map(ServerMeta)` returns database-specific `DataType`
| `VectorType.map()` → `PgType.VECTOR` (PostgreSQL only)

| 3. **TypeHandler Finalization**
| `TypeMappingHandler.apply()` resolves custom/composite/array types
| `"vector"` → `PgType.VECTOR`; `"integer[]"` → `PgType.INTEGER_ARRAY`

| 4. **Value Binding**
| `MappingType.beforeBind()` serializes Java value to SQL parameter
| `VectorType.beforeBind()`: `float[]{0.1,0.2}` → `"[0.1,0.2]"`

| 5. **Value Fetching**
| `MappingType.afterGet()` deserializes database value to Java object
| `VectorType.afterGet()`: `"[0.1,0.2]"` → `float[]{0.1,0.2}`
|===

== Criteria API — Writing SQL

The Criteria API is Army's SQL construction layer.
It generates a database-agnostic statement tree through a type-safe Java DSL, which the dialect parser then translates into native SQL.

=== Standard Criteria API

The Standard Criteria API is Army's database-agnostic SQL construction layer.
It generates an internal statement tree through a type-safe Java DSL, which the dialect parser then translates into native SQL for your target database.

[cols="1,2,2",options="header"]
|===
| Concept | Interface (design) | Implementation

| Entry point | `SQLs` (utility class) | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/SQLs.java[`criteria/impl/SQLs.java`,role="extern"]
| Statement specs | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardInsert.java[`standard/StandardInsert`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardQuery.java[`standard/StandardQuery`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardUpdate.java[`standard/StandardUpdate`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardDelete.java[`standard/StandardDelete`,role="extern"] | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardInserts.java[`impl/StandardInserts`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardQueries.java[`impl/StandardQueries`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardUpdates.java[`impl/StandardUpdates`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardDeletes.java[`impl/StandardDeletes`,role="extern"]
| Standard functions | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/SQLFunction.java[`standard/SQLFunction`,role="extern"] | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/Functions.java[`impl/Functions`,role="extern"]
| Window functions | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/dialect/Window.java[`dialect/Window`,role="extern"] | link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/Windows.java[`impl/Windows`,role="extern"]
|===

==== The SQLs Utility Class

`SQLs` (link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/SQLs.java[role="extern"]) is the unified entry point.
Internally, its static factory methods delegate to `StandardInserts`, `StandardQueries`, `StandardUpdates`, and `StandardDeletes`:

[source,java]
----
// SELECT entry
Select stmt = SQLs.query()...asQuery();

// INSERT entry
Insert stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()...asInsert();

// UPDATE entries
Update stmt = SQLs.singleUpdate()...asUpdate();   // single table
Update stmt = SQLs.domainUpdate()...asUpdate();   // domain (primarily child table)

// DELETE entries
Delete stmt = SQLs.singleDelete()...asDelete();   // single table
Delete stmt = SQLs.domainDelete()...asDelete();   // domain (primarily child table)

// Batch domain variants
BatchUpdate bStmt = SQLs.batchDomainUpdate()...asUpdate().namedParamList(paramList);
BatchDelete bDel = SQLs.batchDomainDelete()...asDelete().namedParamList(paramList);
----

Each returns a type-safe chain that exposes only the clauses valid for that statement type.

==== SELECT Statements

`SQLs.query()` enters the SELECT chain.
Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardQueries.java[`StandardQueries#simpleQuery`,role="extern"], which returns a `StandardQuery.WithSpec`.

===== Basic SELECT

[source,java]
----
final Select stmt;
stmt = SQLs.query()
        .select(Stock_.id, Stock_.name, Stock_.offerPrice)
        .from(Stock_.T, AS, "s")
        .where(Stock_.name.equal("Tesla"))
        .and(Stock_.createTime.less(LocalDateTime.now().minusDays(1)))
        .limit(1)
        .asQuery();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
SELECT s.id, s.name, s.offer_price
FROM stock AS s
WHERE s.name = ?  -- param: 'Tesla'
AND s.create_time < ?  -- param: now - 1 day
LIMIT 1
----

===== Full Clause Chain

The SELECT chain follows SQL clause order:

. `WITH ... AS` — CTE prefix (via `with(name).as(...)`)
. `SELECT` — `select(...)` / `selectDistinct(...)`
. `FROM` — `from(table, AS, alias)` / nested `from(function)`
. `JOIN` — `join(...) / leftJoin(...) / rightJoin(...) / crossJoin(...)`
. `WHERE` — `where(predicate).and(predicate)...`
. `GROUP BY` — `groupBy(...)`
. `HAVING` — `having(predicate)`
. `WINDOW` — `window(name).as(...)` (named window definitions)
. `ORDER BY` — `orderBy(...)`
. `LIMIT / OFFSET` — `limit(n).offset(n)`
. `FOR UPDATE` — `lock(...)` for row-level locking
. `UNION / INTERSECT / EXCEPT` — set operations via `union(...)`, etc.
. `asQuery()` — terminal method, returns `Select`

Each clause method returns the next narrow interface in the chain, so the compiler enforces correct SQL clause ordering.

==== INSERT Statements

===== Single Table INSERT

`SQLs.singleInsert()` returns link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardInsert.java[`StandardInsert._PrimaryOptionSpec<Insert>`,role="extern"].
Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardInserts.java[`StandardInserts#singleInsert`,role="extern"].

*Domain mode* — pass domain objects directly.
Defined in link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._DomainValuesClause`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._DomainValueClause`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardInsert.java[`_ValuesColumnDefaultSpec`,role="extern"]:

[source,java]
----
// (A) Single domain object
//     <TS extends T> R value(TS domain)  →  returns _DmlInsertClause<Insert>
final Insert stmt1;
stmt1 = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)                               // → _ColumnListSpec
        .value(new Stock("GOOGL", "Alphabet"))               // → _DmlInsertClause<Insert>
        .asInsert();                                        // → Insert

// (B) List of domain objects (multi-row)
//     <TS extends T> R values(List<TS> domainList)
final Insert stmt2;
stmt2 = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .defaultValue(Stock_.status, StockStatus.NORMAL)    // optional column default
        .values(stockList)                                   // → _DmlInsertClause<Insert>
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- (A) Single domain: columns follow field declaration order in the document's Stock:
--     id(PRECEDE), create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
--     code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)

-- (B) List with defaultValue: status per-row;
--     when Stock.status is null, 'NORMAL' is substituted
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?),
       (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
----

[cols="1,3,2",options="header"]
|===
| Method | Interface signature | Returns
| `value(TS domain)` | `<TS extends T> R value(TS domain)` in `_DomainValueClause<T,R>` | `_DmlInsertClause<I>` → `.asInsert()`
| `values(List<TS>)` | `<TS extends T> R values(List<TS> domainList)` in `_DomainValuesClause<T,R>` | `_DmlInsertClause<I>` → `.asInsert()`
|===

*Value mode — Static (single row / multi-row)*

Requires `.values()` (no-arg) first — this bridges `_ColumnListSpec` via `_StaticValuesClause` to
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/StandardInsert.java[`StandardInsert._StandardValuesParensClause`,role="extern"], which extends link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._ValuesParensClause`,role="extern"].

Each `parens()` call adds one VALUES row.
All columns are referenced via `FieldMeta` constants.

_Single row:_

[source,java]
----
// .values() → _StandardValuesParensClause
// .parens(Consumer<_StaticValueSpaceClause>) → _ValuesParensCommaSpec → .asInsert()
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .values()                                           // _StaticValuesClause.values() no-arg
        .parens(row -> row                                  // Consumer<_StaticValueSpaceClause<Stock>>
                .space(Stock_.exchange, "NYSE")             //   space(FieldMeta<T>, @Nullable Object)
                .comma(Stock_.code, "AAPL")                 //   comma(FieldMeta<T>, @Nullable Object)
                .comma(Stock_.name, SQLs::param, "Alphabet")//   comma(FieldMeta, BiFunction, E) — binding
                .ifComma(Stock_.offerPrice, offerValue)     //   conditional comma — skipped when null
        )
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Value mode always inserts ALL table columns; fields not explicitly set
-- use DEFAULT (NullMode.DEFAULT→INSERT_DEFAULT for PostgreSQL)
-- id, create_time, update_time, version are managed by Army
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, ?,          -- offer_price uses DEFAULT when offerValue is null
        DEFAULT)           -- listing_date uses DEFAULT
-- params: id(snowflake), 'NYSE', 'AAPL', ?(param: 'Alphabet'), offerValue
----

._StaticValueSpaceClause methods:
[cols="1,3",options="header"]
|===
| Method | Signature
| `space(field, value)` | First pair; `value` can be literal, `Expression`, `null`, or `SQLs.DEFAULT`
| `space(field, funcRef, value)` | First pair with binding: `SQLs::param`
| `spaceIf(field, value)` | Conditional first pair — skipped when `value` is `null`
| `spaceIf(field, funcRef, value)` | Conditional first pair with binding
| `comma(field, value)` | Subsequent pair
| `comma(field, funcRef, value)` | Subsequent pair with binding
| `ifComma(field, value)` | Conditional subsequent pair
| `ifComma(field, funcRef, value)` | Conditional subsequent pair with binding
|===

_Multi-row — chain via `.comma()`:_

[source,java]
----
// .parens() → _ValuesParensCommaSpec  →  .comma() loops back
// _ValuesParensCommaSpec extends _CommaClause<_StandardValuesParensClause>
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .values()
        .parens(r -> r                                   // row 1
                .space(Stock_.exchange, "NYSE")
                .comma(Stock_.code, "AAPL")
                .comma(Stock_.name, "Apple Inc.")
        )
        .comma()                                           // → back to _StandardValuesParensClause
        .parens(r -> r                                    // row 2
                .space(Stock_.exchange, "NASDAQ")
                .comma(Stock_.code, "GOOGL")
                .comma(Stock_.name, SQLs::param, "Alphabet")
        )
        .comma()
        .parens(r -> r                                    // row 3 (conditional first column)
                .spaceIf(Stock_.exchange, exchangeValue)   // skipped if exchangeValue == null
                .comma(Stock_.code, "MSFT")
                .comma(Stock_.name, "Microsoft")
        )
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Default mode: all table columns appear in the INSERT list.
-- id, create_time, update_time, version managed by Army;
-- unset nullable fields → DEFAULT (NullMode.DEFAULT→INSERT_DEFAULT for PostgreSQL)
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT),         -- row 1: 'NYSE', 'AAPL', 'Apple Inc.'
       (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT),         -- row 2: 'NASDAQ', 'GOOGL', ? (param: 'Alphabet')
       (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT)          -- row 3: exchangeValue non-null→param, null→DEFAULT; 'MSFT', 'Microsoft'
----

*Value mode — Dynamic (multi-row via `ValuesConstructor`)*

Defined in link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._DynamicValuesClause`,role="extern"]:
`values(Consumer<ValuesConstructor<T>>)`.
Returns `_DmlInsertClause<I>`.

link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/ValuesConstructor.java[`ValuesConstructor<T>`,role="extern"]
extends link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`_ValuesParensClause<T,_CommaClause<ValuesConstructor<T>>>`,role="extern"].
Each `parens()` returns a comma clause; `.comma()` chains back to `ValuesConstructor`.

Inside `parens()`, there are *two* sub-modes:

_Static row — type-safe via `FieldMeta` (same `_StaticValueSpaceClause` as above):_

[source,java]
----
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .values(rows -> rows                                // Consumer<ValuesConstructor<Stock>>
                .parens(r -> r                           // Consumer<_StaticValueSpaceClause<Stock>>
                        .space(Stock_.exchange, "NYSE")    //   space(FieldMeta<T>, Object)
                        .comma(Stock_.code, "AAPL")
                        .comma(Stock_.name, "Apple Inc.")
                )
                .comma()                                    // → back to ValuesConstructor
               .parens(SQLs.SPACE,s-> {   // row 2   dynamic column
                        s.set(Stock_.exchange, "NASDAQ");
                        s.set(Stock_.code, "GOOGL");
                        s.set(Stock_.name, SQLs::param, "Alphabet"); // set with binding
                })
        )
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT),        -- row 1: 'NYSE', 'AAPL', 'Apple Inc.'
       (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT)         -- row 2: 'NASDAQ', 'GOOGL', ? (param: 'Alphabet')
----

_Dynamic row — via `Assignments` (uses `set()` instead of `space()`/`comma()`):_

[source,java]
----
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .values(rows -> rows                                // Consumer<ValuesConstructor<Stock>>
                .parens(s -> s                  // Consumer<Assignments<Stock>>
                        .space(Stock_.exchange, "NYSE")       //   space(FieldMeta<T>, @Nullable Object)
                        .comma(Stock_.code, "AAPL")           //   each set() returns Assignments<T>
                        .comma(Stock_.name, "Apple Inc.")
                        .ifComma(Stock_.offerPrice, offer)    //   conditional — skipped when null
                )
                .comma()
                .parens(SQLs.SPACE,s-> {   // row 2   dynamic column
                        s.set(Stock_.exchange, "NASDAQ");
                        s.set(Stock_.code, "GOOGL");
                        s.set(Stock_.name, SQLs::param, "Alphabet"); // set with binding
                })
        )
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock (id, create_time, update_time, version, exchange,
                   code, name, status, offer_price, listing_date)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, ?,           -- row 1: offer_price uses DEFAULT when offer is null
        DEFAULT),
       (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
        DEFAULT)
-- row 1: 'NYSE', 'AAPL', 'Apple Inc.', offer
-- row 2: 'NASDAQ', 'GOOGL', ? (param: 'Alphabet')
----

`Assignments` extends link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._StaticAssignmentSetClause`,role="extern"]:

[cols="1,3",options="header"]
|===
| Method | Signature
| `set(field, value)` | `R set(FieldMeta<T>, @Nullable Object)` — literal, Expression, or null
| `set(field, funcRef, value)` | `<E> R set(FieldMeta<T>, BiFunction<...,Expression>, @Nullable E)` — with binding
| `ifSet(field, value)` | `R ifSet(FieldMeta<T>, @Nullable Object)` — conditional, skipped when null
| `ifSet(field, funcRef, value)` | `<E> R ifSet(FieldMeta<T>, BiFunction<...,Expression>, @Nullable E)` — conditional with binding
|===

TIP: The _Static row_ sub-mode uses the same `_StaticValueSpaceClause` lambdas as the non-Dynamic path.
The _Dynamic row_ sub-mode uses `Assignments.set()` which is useful when columns are added in a loop or conditionally.

*Query mode* — insert from a subquery.
Defined in link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._QueryInsertSpaceClause`,role="extern"] +
link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._ColumnListParensClause`,role="extern"].

`_ColumnListParensClause` has two `parens()` overloads for specifying the target column list.
`_QueryInsertSpaceClause` has three `space()` overloads for providing the subquery source.

[cols="1,3,2",options="header"]
|===
| Signal | Method | Returns
| static columns | `parens(Consumer<_StaticColumnSpaceClause<T>>)` | `_ComplexColumnDefaultSpec`
| dynamic columns | `parens(SQLs.SymbolSpace, Consumer<Consumer<FieldMeta<T>>>)` | `_ComplexColumnDefaultSpec`
| pre-built subquery | `space(Supplier<SubQuery>)` | `_DmlInsertClause<I>`
| inline via function | `space(Function<SelectSpec, _DmlInsertClause<I>>)` | `_DmlInsertClause<I>`
| bare `space()` | `T space()` | `SelectSpec<_DmlInsertClause<I>>` → chain `.asInsert()`
|===

_Form 1 — Static columns + pre-built SubQuery:_

[source,java]
----
// _StaticColumnSpaceClause: space(f1,f2) — 1/2/4 column params supported
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .parens(cols -> cols                                // Consumer<_StaticColumnSpaceClause<Stock>>
                .space(Stock_.exchange, Stock_.code)        //   space(FieldMeta, FieldMeta) → _StaticColumnDualClause
                .comma(Stock_.name)                         //   comma(FieldMeta)
        )
        .space(subQuery)                                    // SQLs.subQuery()...asQuery() → subQuery
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock (exchange, code, name, id, create_time,
                   update_time, version)
SELECT ...  -- subQuery SQL; append  Army-managed fields (id, create_time, update_time, version)
----

_Form 2 — Dynamic columns + pre-built SubQuery:_

[source,java]
----
// Dynamic column list: each accept(field) adds one column
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .parens(SQLs.SPACE, list -> {                       // Consumer<Consumer<FieldMeta<Stock>>>
                list.accept(Stock_.exchange);                //   accept(FieldMeta<T>)
                list.accept(Stock_.code);
                list.accept(Stock_.name);
        })
        .space(subQuery)                              // SQLs.subQuery()...asQuery()
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock (exchange, code, name, id, create_time,
                   update_time, version)
SELECT ...  -- subQuery SQL; Army-managed fields (id, create_time, update_time, version)
-- are appended to column list; all column values come from the subquery
----

_Form 3 — No column list (subquery determines columns):_

[source,java]
----
// Direct .space(subQuery) on _ComplexColumnDefaultSpec — no parens() needed
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .space(subQuery)                                    // _QueryInsertSpaceClause.space(Supplier)
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock
SELECT ...  -- subQuery determines all columns
----

_Form 4 — No-arg `space()` returns `SelectSpec` (advanced):_

[source,java]
----
// space() no-arg → SelectSpec<_DmlInsertClause<Insert>>
// Build subquery inline, chain ends with .asInsert()
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(Stock_.T)
        .parens(cols -> cols.space(Stock_.exchange, Stock_.code, Stock_.name, Stock_.status))
        .space()                                            // T space() → SelectSpec
        .select(Stock_.exchange, Stock_.code, Stock_.name)
        .from(NasdaqTable_.T, AS, "n")
        .where(NasdaqTable_.listed.equal(true))
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
INSERT INTO stock (exchange, code, name, status, id, create_time,
                   update_time, version)
SELECT n.exchange, n.code, n.name, DEFAULT, DEFAULT, DEFAULT,
       DEFAULT, DEFAULT
FROM nasdaq_table AS n
WHERE n.listed = ?  -- param: true
-- status: DB column default (not in user SELECT)
-- id, create_time, update_time, version: appended by Army, all values from the subquery
----

===== Child INSERT (Parent-Child Hierarchy)

When using `@Inheritance` single-table inheritance, a *parent insert* must be followed by a *child insert*.
This is enforced at the interface level:
`insertInto(ParentTableMeta)` returns a chain that ends with `child()` to enter the child table's insert.

Internally, `StandardInserts` handles this via link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardInserts.java[`_ChildInsertIntoClause`,role="extern"]
and link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/InsertStatement.java[`InsertStatement._ParentInsert20`,role="extern"]:

[source,java]
----
// Parent insert → child insert chain
final Insert stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleInsert()
        .insertInto(ParentUser_.T)         // ParentTableMeta — returns _ParentInsert20
        .defaultValue(ParentUser_.status, UserStatus.ADMIN)
        .values(parentUserList)
        .child()                            // enters child insert context
        .insertInto(Admin_.T)              // ChildTableMeta — returns _ColumnListSpec
        .values(adminUserList)
        .asInsert();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Statement 1: parent rows (no discriminator column)
--     Columns follow field declaration order in ParentUser class:
--     1. Army managed fields: id, create_time, update_time, version
--     2. Parent business fields: name
INSERT INTO u_parent_user (id, create_time, update_time, version, name)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?),
       ...

-- Statement 2: child rows (includes discriminator column)
--     Columns follow field declaration order in Admin class:
--     1. id (mandatory, first position; child id always managed by Army)
--     2. Child-specific fields: admin_level, role
--     discriminator 'ADMIN' from @DiscriminatorValue is auto-injected
INSERT INTO u_admin (id, admin_level, role, status)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?),
       ...

-- NOTE: For parent/simple tables, when id GeneratorType is POST (database
--       auto-increment), the id column is NOT included in the column list.
--       Child tables ALWAYS include id regardless of GeneratorType.
----

[TIP]
====
The `child()` method is only available when the previous `insertInto()` received a `ParentTableMeta`.
Army generates separate `INSERT` statements for parent and child tables internally.
====

===== INSERT Options

[cols="1,3,2",options="header"]
|===
| Option | Interface (from `InsertStatement`) | Chain position
| `literalMode(mode)` | `_PreferLiteralClause` — reduce placeholders for large batches | before `insertInto()`
| `nullMode(mode)` | `_NullOptionClause` — control NULL handling | before `insertInto()`
| `migration()` | `_MigrationOptionClause` — migration mode for schema transfer | before `insertInto()`
| `ignoreReturnIds()` | `_IgnoreReturnIdsOptionClause` — skip ID return for conflict clauses | before `insertInto()`
|===

==== UPDATE Statements

===== Single Table UPDATE

`SQLs.singleUpdate()` enters the UPDATE chain.
Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardUpdates.java[`StandardUpdates#singleUpdate`,role="extern"].

[source,java]
----
final Update stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleUpdate()
        .update(Stock_.T, AS, "s")         // SingleTableMeta — requires alias
        .set(Stock_.name, "Tesla")
        .set(Stock_.offerPrice, SQLs::plusEqual, addPrice)
        .where(Stock_.id.between(map.get("firstId"), SQLs.AND, map.get("secondId")))
        .asUpdate();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
UPDATE stock AS s
SET name = ?,
    offer_price = s.offer_price + ?,
    update_time = ?,
    version = s.version + 1
WHERE s.id BETWEEN ? AND ?
----

The `set()` method comes from link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/UpdateStatement.java[`UpdateStatement._StaticSetClause`,role="extern"].
It supports value operators like `SQLs::plusEqual`, `SQLs::minusEqual`, etc., and `setRow()` for multi-column subquery assignment.

===== Domain UPDATE

`SQLs.domainUpdate()` is primarily designed for child tables in `@Inheritance` single-table inheritance hierarchies.
It accepts `ChildTableMeta` — allowing updates to a domain object's fields including those inherited from parent classes, all in a single `UPDATE` statement against the shared table.
It also works with `SingleTableMeta` for plain single-table domains.

`SQLs.batchDomainUpdate()` is the batch variant, returning `_DomainUpdateClause<_BatchUpdateParamSpec>` — chain `.namedParamList(paramList)` after `.asUpdate()` to get `BatchUpdate`.

Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardUpdates.java[`StandardUpdates#simpleDomain` / `StandardUpdates#batchDomain`,role="extern"].

_Child table domain UPDATE_ (primary use case):

[source,java]
----
// Admin child table inherits from User (see @Inheritance / @DiscriminatorValue)
// Admin_.T is ChildTableMeta — mapped to u_admin
final Update stmt;
stmt = SQLs.domainUpdate()
        .update(Admin_.T, AS, "a")         // ChildTableMeta — can reference parent fields
        .set(Admin_.adminLevel, 5)              // child-specific field: triggers CTE/multi-table path
        .set(ParentUser_.name, "Admin User")    // parent field: name
        .set(ParentUser_.visible, false)         // parent field: visible (soft delete)
        .where(Admin_.id.equal(1L))
        .asUpdate();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Domain UPDATE on child table Admin_.T:
-- PostgreSQL uses CTE-based two-stage update:
--   1. CTE: UPDATE child table child-specific fields + RETURNING id
--   2. Main: UPDATE parent table fields FROM cte
WITH a_update_cte AS (
    UPDATE u_admin AS a
    SET admin_level = ?
    FROM u_parent_user AS p_of_a
    WHERE a.id = p_of_a.id         -- join condition (first)
    AND p_of_a.id = ?  -- param: 1
    AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected
    AND p_of_a.visible = true    -- visible auto-filtered
    RETURNING a.id AS id
)
UPDATE u_parent_user AS p_of_a
SET name = ?,
    visible = ?,
    update_time = ?,
    version = p_of_a.version + 1
FROM a_update_cte
WHERE p_of_a.id = a_update_cte.id
----

.Generated SQL (MySQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Domain UPDATE on child table Admin_.T:
-- MySQL uses multi-table UPDATE syntax:
--   UPDATE <child> JOIN <parent> ON ... SET ...
UPDATE u_admin AS a
JOIN u_parent_user AS p_of_a ON a.id = p_of_a.id
SET p_of_a.name = ?,
    p_of_a.visible = ?,
    a.admin_level = ?,
    p_of_a.update_time = ?,
    p_of_a.version = p_of_a.version + 1
WHERE p_of_a.id = ?  -- param: 1
AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected
AND p_of_a.visible = true    -- visible auto-filtered
----

_Batch domain UPDATE (child table):_

[source,java]
----
final BatchUpdate stmt;
List<Map<String, Object>> paramList = List.of(
    Map.of("name", "Alice", "adminLevel", 5, "id", 1L),
    Map.of("name", "Bob", "adminLevel", 3, "id", 2L)
);
stmt = SQLs.batchDomainUpdate()
        .update(Admin_.T, AS, "a")
        .sets(pairs -> pairs
                .setSpace(ParentUser_.name, SQLs::namedParam)
                .setSpace(Admin_.adminLevel, SQLs::namedParam)   -- child field → triggers CTE/multi-table
        )
        .where(Admin_.id.spaceEqual(SQLs::namedParam))
        .asUpdate()
        .namedParamList(paramList);

long rows = session.update(stmt);
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Batch domain UPDATE on child table Admin_.T:
-- PostgreSQL uses CTE-based two-stage update
WITH a_update_cte AS (
    UPDATE u_admin AS a
    SET admin_level = ?              -- batch param: adminLevel
    FROM u_parent_user AS p_of_a
    WHERE a.id = p_of_a.id           -- join condition (first)
    AND p_of_a.id = ?              -- batch param: id (user WHERE before Army managed)
    AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected (appended)
    AND p_of_a.visible = true      -- visible auto-filtered (appended)
    RETURNING a.id AS id
)
UPDATE u_parent_user AS p_of_a
SET name = ?,                       -- batch param: name
    update_time = ?,
    version = p_of_a.version + 1
FROM a_update_cte
WHERE p_of_a.id = a_update_cte.id
----

.Generated SQL (MySQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Batch domain UPDATE on child table Admin_.T:
-- MySQL uses multi-table UPDATE syntax
UPDATE u_admin AS a
JOIN u_parent_user AS p_of_a ON a.id = p_of_a.id
SET p_of_a.name = ?,               -- batch param: name
    a.admin_level = ?,              -- batch param: adminLevel
    p_of_a.update_time = ?,
    p_of_a.version = p_of_a.version + 1
WHERE p_of_a.id = ?                  -- batch param: id (user WHERE before Army managed)
AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'      -- discriminator auto-injected (appended)
AND p_of_a.visible = true          -- visible auto-filtered (appended)
----

_Single-table domain UPDATE_ (also supported):

[source,java]
----
final Update stmt;
stmt = SQLs.domainUpdate()
        .update(Stock_.T, "s")              // TableMeta — no AS keyword
        .set(Stock_.name, "Tesla")
        .where(Stock_.id.equal(100L))
        .asUpdate();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
UPDATE stock s
SET name = ?,
    update_time = ?,
    version = s.version + 1
WHERE s.id = ?  -- param: 100
----

[cols="1,3",options="header"]
|===
| Entry Point | Description
| `SQLs.singleUpdate()` | Standard UPDATE with table alias; `update(SingleTableMeta, AS, alias)` — single table only
| `SQLs.domainUpdate()` | Domain UPDATE — primarily for child tables; accepts `ChildTableMeta` / `TableMeta` / `SingleTableMeta`
| `SQLs.batchDomainUpdate()` | Batch domain UPDATE; returns `_DomainUpdateClause<_BatchUpdateParamSpec>` — chain `.namedParamList()`
|===

===== Batch Single Table UPDATE

For batch operations on a single table with named parameters:

[source,java]
----
final BatchUpdate stmt;
List<Map<String, Object>> paramList = List.of(
    Map.of("name", "Tesla", "offerPrice", 250, "id", 1),
    Map.of("name", "Apple", "offerPrice", 180, "id", 2)
);
stmt = SQLs.batchSingleUpdate()
        .update(Stock_.T, AS, "s")
        .sets(pairs -> pairs
                .setSpace(Stock_.name, SQLs::namedParam)      // named param placeholder
                .setSpace(Stock_.offerPrice, SQLs::namedParam) // named param placeholder
        )
        .where(Stock_.id.spaceEqual(SQLs::namedParam))       // space* methods for named params
        .asUpdate()
        .namedParamList(paramList);

// Execute batch
long rows = session.update(stmt);
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Batch 1: name='Tesla', offerPrice=250, id=1
UPDATE stock AS s
SET name = ?,
    offer_price = ?,
    update_time = ?,
    version = s.version + 1
WHERE s.id = ?

-- Batch 2: name='Apple', offerPrice=180, id=2
-- (same SQL structure, different parameter values)
----

==== DELETE Statements

===== Single Table DELETE

`SQLs.singleDelete()` enters the DELETE chain.
Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardDeletes.java[`StandardDeletes#singleDelete`,role="extern"].

[source,java]
----
final Delete stmt;
stmt = SQLs.singleDelete()
        .deleteFrom(Stock_.T, AS, "s")      // SingleTableMeta — requires alias
        .where(Stock_.status.equal(StockStatus.DELISTED))
        .asDelete();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
DELETE FROM stock AS s
WHERE s.status = ?  -- param: 'DELISTED'
----

===== Domain DELETE

`SQLs.domainDelete()` is primarily designed for child tables in `@Inheritance` single-table inheritance hierarchies.
It accepts `TableMeta` (including `ChildTableMeta`) — so you can delete domain objects from a child table, with the discriminator value automatically filtered.
It also works with `SingleTableMeta` for plain single-table domains.

`SQLs.batchDomainDelete()` is the batch variant, returning `_DomainDeleteClause<_BatchDeleteParamSpec>` — chain `.namedParamList(paramList)` after `.asDelete()` to get `BatchDelete`.

Internally it calls link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/StandardDeletes.java[`StandardDeletes#domainDelete` / `StandardDeletes#batchDomainDelete`,role="extern"].

_Child table domain DELETE_ (primary use case):

[source,java]
----
// Admin child table inherits from User — Admin_.T is ChildTableMeta — mapped to u_admin
final Delete stmt;
stmt = SQLs.domainDelete()
        .deleteFrom(Admin_.T, AS, "a")     // ChildTableMeta
        .where(ParentUser_.visible.equal(false))  // parent field: visible
        .asDelete();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Domain DELETE on child table Admin_.T:
-- PostgreSQL uses CTE-based two-stage delete:
--   1. CTE: DELETE child rows + RETURNING child IDs
--   2. Main: DELETE parent rows matched by returned IDs
-- discriminator is applied in CTE WHERE on parent alias "p_of_a"
WITH a_delete_cte AS (
    DELETE FROM u_admin AS a
    USING u_parent_user AS p_of_a
    WHERE a.id = p_of_a.id         -- join condition (first)
    AND p_of_a.visible = ?  -- param: false (0)
    AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected
    AND p_of_a.visible = true    -- visible auto-filtered
    RETURNING a.id AS id
)
DELETE FROM u_parent_user AS p_of_a
USING a_delete_cte
WHERE p_of_a.id = a_delete_cte.id
----

.Generated SQL (MySQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Domain DELETE on child table Admin_.T:
-- MySQL uses multi-table DELETE syntax:
--   DELETE <child_alias>, <parent_alias> FROM <child> JOIN <parent> WHERE ...
-- discriminator is applied in WHERE on parent alias "p_of_a"
DELETE a, p_of_a
FROM u_admin AS a
JOIN u_parent_user AS p_of_a ON a.id = p_of_a.id
WHERE p_of_a.visible = ?  -- param: false (0)
AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected
AND p_of_a.visible = true    -- visible auto-filtered
----

_Batch domain DELETE (child table):_

[source,java]
----
final BatchDelete stmt;
List<Map<String, Object>> paramList = List.of(
    Map.of("id", 1L),
    Map.of("id", 2L)
);
stmt = SQLs.batchDomainDelete()
        .deleteFrom(Admin_.T, AS, "a")
        .where(Admin_.id.spaceEqual(SQLs::namedParam))
        .asDelete()
        .namedParamList(paramList);

long rows = session.update(stmt);
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Batch domain DELETE on child table Admin_.T:
-- PostgreSQL uses CTE-based two-stage delete
-- user WHERE condition contains named parameter "id"
WITH a_delete_cte AS (
    DELETE FROM u_admin AS a
    USING u_parent_user AS p_of_a
    WHERE a.id = p_of_a.id           -- join condition (first)
    AND a.id = ?                   -- batch param: id (user WHERE before Army managed)
    AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected (appended)
    AND p_of_a.visible = true      -- visible auto-filtered (appended)
    RETURNING a.id AS id
)
DELETE FROM u_parent_user AS p_of_a
USING a_delete_cte
WHERE p_of_a.id = a_delete_cte.id
----

.Generated SQL (MySQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Batch domain DELETE on child table Admin_.T:
-- MySQL uses multi-table DELETE syntax
-- user WHERE condition contains named parameter "id"
DELETE a, p_of_a
FROM u_admin AS a
JOIN u_parent_user AS p_of_a ON a.id = p_of_a.id
WHERE a.id = ?                   -- batch param: id (user WHERE before Army managed)
AND p_of_a.status = 'ADMIN'  -- discriminator auto-injected (appended)
AND p_of_a.visible = true      -- visible auto-filtered (appended)
----

_Single-table domain DELETE_ (also supported):

[source,java]
----
final Delete stmt;
stmt = SQLs.domainDelete()
        .deleteFrom(Stock_.T, AS, "s")      // TableMeta — any table type
        .where(Stock_.visible.equal(false))
        .asDelete();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
DELETE FROM stock AS s
WHERE s.visible = ?  -- param: false (0)
----

All base interfaces for DELETE are defined in link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/DeleteStatement.java[`DeleteStatement`,role="extern"]:

[cols="1,2",options="header"]
|===
| Clause | Interface
| Single-table | `_SingleDeleteFromClause` / `_SingleDeleteClause`
| Parent table | `_DeleteParentClause`
| Child table | `_DeleteChildClause`
|===

==== Standard Functions

Army provides standard SQL functions through the `Functions` utility class (link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/Functions.java[`impl/Functions.java`,role="extern"]).
All standard function interfaces are declared in link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/standard/SQLFunction.java[`standard/SQLFunction.java`,role="extern"].

Functions can be used anywhere an `Expression` is expected — in `SELECT`, `WHERE`, `ORDER BY`, `GROUP BY`, and `HAVING`.

===== Aggregate Functions

[cols="1,3",options="header"]
|===
| Function | Signature
| `COUNT(*)` | `SQLs.count(SQLs.ASTERISK)`
| `COUNT(expr)` | `SQLs.count(expr)`
| `COUNT(DISTINCT expr)` | `SQLs.count(SQLs.DISTINCT, expr)`
| `SUM(expr)` | `SQLs.sum(expr)`, `SQLs.sum(SQLs.DISTINCT, expr)`
| `AVG(expr)` | `SQLs.avg(expr)`, `SQLs.avg(SQLs.DISTINCT, expr)`
| `MIN(expr)` | `SQLs.min(expr)`
| `MAX(expr)` | `SQLs.max(expr)`
|===

[source,java]
----
// Aggregate in SELECT
stmt = SQLs.query()
        .select(Stock_.exchange, SQLs.count(SQLs.ASTERISK))
        .from(Stock_.T, AS, "s")
        .groupBy(Stock_.exchange)
        .asQuery();

// Aggregate in HAVING
stmt = SQLs.query()
        .select(Stock_.exchange, SQLs.count(SQLs.ASTERISK))
        .from(Stock_.T, AS, "s")
        .groupBy(Stock_.exchange)
        .having(SQLs.count(SQLs.ASTERISK).greater(100))
        .asQuery();
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Aggregate in SELECT
SELECT s.exchange, COUNT(*)
FROM stock AS s
GROUP BY s.exchange

-- Aggregate in HAVING
SELECT s.exchange, COUNT(*)
FROM stock AS s
GROUP BY s.exchange
HAVING COUNT(*) > 100
----

===== Scalar Functions

Army provides the full range of standard SQL scalar functions:

*Math functions* — `acos`, `asin`, `atan`, `atan2`, `ceil`, `cos`, `floor`, `ln`, `log`, `mod`, `power`, `round`, `sign`, `sqrt`, `truncate`, etc.

*String functions* — `length`, `lower`, `upper`, `trim`, `substring`, etc. (also `concat` via dialect API)

*Datetime functions* — `extract`, `currentDate`, `currentTime`, etc. (available via dialect API)

*Conditional functions* — `coalesce`, `nullif` (available via dialect API)

*CASE expression* — `SQLs.cases()` / `SQLs.cases(expr)` + `.when(...).then(...).elseValue(...).end(type)`

[source,java]
----
// Math: ROUND(offer_price, 2) > 100
Stock_.offerPrice.greater(SQLs.round(Stock_.offerPrice, 2))

// String: LENGTH(code)
SQLs.length(Stock_.code)

// Math: POWER(offer_price, 2)
SQLs.pow(Stock_.offerPrice, 2)

// CASE: price category
SQLs.cases()
         .when(Stock_.offerPrice.greater(1000)).then("HIGH")
         .when(Stock_.offerPrice.greater(100)).then("MID")
         .elseValue("LOW")
         .end(StandardInfer.STRING)
----

For the complete function reference, see link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/Functions.java[`Functions.java`,role="extern"].

==== Standard Window Functions

Window functions are provided through the `Windows` utility class (link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/impl/Windows.java[`impl/Windows.java`,role="extern"]), implementing link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/dialect/Window.java[`dialect/Window`,role="extern"].

Unlike aggregate functions, window functions require an `OVER` clause which specifies partitioning, ordering, and framing.

[cols="1,2,2",options="header"]
|===
| Function | Signature | Return Type
| `ROW_NUMBER()` | `Windows.rowNumber()` | `LongType`
| `RANK()` | (use dialect API) | —
| `DENSE_RANK()` | `Windows.denseRank()` | `LongType`
| `NTILE(n)` | `Windows.ntile(n)` | `LongType`
| `CUME_DIST()` | `Windows.cumeDist()` | `DoubleType`
| `LAG(expr)` | `Windows.lag(expr)` | Same as `expr`
| `LAG(expr, n)` | `Windows.lag(expr, n)` | Same as `expr`
| `LAG(expr, n, default)` | `Windows.lag(expr, n, default)` | Same as `expr`
| `LEAD(expr)` | `Windows.lead(expr)` | Same as `expr`
| `LEAD(expr, n)` | `Windows.lead(expr, n)` | Same as `expr`
| `LEAD(expr, n, default)` | `Windows.lead(expr, n, default)` | Same as `expr`
| `FIRST_VALUE(expr)` | `Windows.firstValue(expr)` | Same as `expr`
| `LAST_VALUE(expr)` | `Windows.lastValue(expr)` | Same as `expr`
| `NTH_VALUE(expr, n)` | `Windows.nthValue(expr, n)` | Same as `expr`
|===

Each window function returns a `Windows._OverSpec` (or `Windows._WindowAggSpec` for aggregate windows), which exposes the `over()` methods defined by link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/dialect/Window.java[`Window._OverWindowClause`,role="extern"]:

[source,java]
----
// Simple OVER()
Windows.rowNumber().over()

// OVER with named window definition
Windows.rowNumber().over("w")

// OVER with inline PARTITION BY + ORDER BY
Windows.rowNumber().over(w -> w
        .partitionBy(Stock_.exchange)
        .orderBy(Stock_.offerPrice.desc())
)

// LAG with offset and default
Windows.lag(Stock_.offerPrice, 1, 0)
     .over(w -> w.partitionBy(Stock_.exchange).orderBy(Stock_.createTime.asc()))

// Aggregate window: SUM over a sliding frame
SQLs.sum(Stock_.offerPrice)
         .over(w -> w
                 .partitionBy(Stock_.exchange)
                 .orderBy(Stock_.createTime.asc())
                 .rowsBetween(
                         Window._FrameUnit.UNBOUNDED_PRECEDING,
                         Window._FrameUnit.CURRENT_ROW
                 )
         )
----

[NOTE]
====
**Aggregate functions as window functions:** `SQLs.sum(expr)`, `SQLs.avg(expr)`, etc.
can also be used with `.over(...)` — they become window aggregates.
When used without `.over()`, they remain standard aggregates (require `GROUP BY`).
====

=== Expression(s)

In Army, "everything" is an `Expression` — a design philosophy where every participant in SQL statement construction shares this single interface.
Whether it is a literal value, a bound parameter, a table column, a function call, or a subquery, they all conform to the `Expression` contract, enabling uniform composition, type inference, and SQL generation.

The following all implement `Expression`:

- Plain `Expression` objects (the interface itself) — the polymorphic root
- JDBC `?` parameters (`SQLs.param(field, value)`) — see <<Parameter Binding>>
- Literal values (`SQLs.literalValue(100)`, `SQLs.constValue("text")`) — see <<Literal Binding>>
- SQL functions (`SQLs.sum(expr)`, `SQLs.length(expr)`) — see <<Scalar Functions>>
- Identifiers (`SQLs.identifier("alias")`)
- Table columns — metamodel fields such as `Stock_.offerPrice`
- Composite type fields (`compositeExpr.dot("field_name")`)
- Row (`SQLs.row()`)
- Array expressions (`scores.slice(1, SQLs.COLON, 5)`)
- Scalar subqueries (`SQLs.scalarSubQuery()`)

The `Expression` interface declares all operations a SQL expression can participate in — comparison, arithmetic, bitwise, pattern matching, array slicing, type casting, sorting, and more.

==== Expression

===== equal

The `=` operator.
The right side can be a Java literal, another `Expression`, or `null`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.status.equal(StockStatus.NORMAL)
Stock_.name.equal(Stock_.exchange)     // field-to-field comparison
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"status" = ?              -- param: NORMAL
"name" = "exchange"
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== notEqual

The `<>` operator.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.code.notEqual("000001")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"code" <> ?               -- param: '000001'
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== nullSafeEqual

`IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` — treats `NULL` as a comparable value (`@Support({MySQL, PostgreSQL, H2})`).

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.nullSafeEqual(SQLs.NULL)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" IS NOT DISTINCT FROM NULL
----

[TIP]
====
`SQLs.NULL` is an `Expression` — no implicit wrapping occurs.
For null-as-parameter use `field.nullSafeEqual(SQLs::param, null)` (`TypedExpression`).
See <<parameter()>> for parameterized null binding.
====

.Generated SQL (MySQL)
[source,sql]
----
offer_price <=> NULL
----

===== less

The `<` operator.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.less(new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" < ?             -- param: 100.00
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== lessEqual

The `<=` operator.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.version.lessEqual(10)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"version" <= ?             -- param: 10
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== greater

The `>` operator.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.greater(new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" > ?             -- param: 100.00
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== greaterEqual

The `>=` operator.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.listingDate.greaterEqual(LocalDate.of(2024, 1, 1))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"listing_date" >= ?            -- param: 2024-01-01
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== between

`BETWEEN ... AND ...` range comparison.
PostgreSQL additionally supports `SYMMETRIC` / `ASYMMETRIC` modifier overloads.

[source,java]
----
// Basic usage
Stock_.offerPrice.between(new BigDecimal("10.00"), SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("100.00"))

// PostgreSQL SYMMETRIC — auto-swaps bounds so lower <= upper
Stock_.offerPrice.between(SQLs.SYMMETRIC, new BigDecimal("100.00"),
        SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("10.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" BETWEEN ? AND ?            -- params: 10.00, 100.00
"offer_price" BETWEEN SYMMETRIC ? AND ?  -- params: 100.00, 10.00 (auto-swapped)
----

[TIP]
====
Both bound values are implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing JDBC `?` placeholders.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== notBetween

`NOT BETWEEN ... AND ...` range exclusion.
Also supports `SYMMETRIC` / `ASYMMETRIC` modifiers.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.notBetween(new BigDecimal("10.00"), SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" NOT BETWEEN ? AND ?         -- params: 10.00, 100.00
----

[TIP]
====
Both bound values are implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing JDBC `?` placeholders.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== is

`IS` boolean test — accepts `BoolTestWord` (`TRUE`/`FALSE`/`UNKNOWN`/`NULL`) or PostgreSQL's `IsComparisonWord` (`DISTINCT FROM`).

[source,java]
----
// Boolean test
SQLs.exists(subQuery).is(SQLs.TRUE)

// PostgreSQL: IS DISTINCT FROM
Stock_.name.is(SQLs.DISTINCT_FROM, SQLs.parameter(null))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
EXISTS (SELECT ...) IS TRUE
"name" IS DISTINCT FROM ?    -- param: null
----

[TIP]
====
`BoolTestWord` values (`TRUE`/`FALSE`/`UNKNOWN`/`NULL`) are `Expression` instances — no implicit wrapping occurs. `IsComparisonWord` operands (e.g. `SQLs.DISTINCT_FROM` + value) go through `wrapRight`; for null use `SQLs.NULL` instead of `SQLs.parameter(null)`.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== isNot

`IS NOT` boolean test — the negated counterpart of `is`.

[source,java]
----
SQLs.exists(subQuery).isNot(SQLs.FALSE)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
EXISTS (SELECT ...) IS NOT FALSE
----

[TIP]
====
`BoolTestWord` operands are already `Expression` instances — no implicit wrapping.
See <<parameter()>> for explicit parameter binding.
====

===== isNull

`IS NULL`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.isNull()
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" IS NULL
----

===== isNotNull

`IS NOT NULL`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.name.isNotNull()
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"name" IS NOT NULL
----

===== like

`LIKE` pattern matching.
Supports `ESCAPE` clause for escaping wildcards.

[source,java]
----
// Basic fuzzy match
Stock_.name.like("%Apple%")

// With ESCAPE
Stock_.code.like("100\\_%", SQLs.ESCAPE, "\\")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"name" LIKE ?               -- param: '%Apple%'
"code" LIKE ? ESCAPE ?      -- params: '100\_%', '\'
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== notLike

`NOT LIKE` negated pattern matching.
Also supports `ESCAPE`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.name.notLike("%invalid%")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"name" NOT LIKE ?           -- param: '%invalid%'
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== similarTo

PostgreSQL `SIMILAR TO` — SQL-standard regex matching (`@Support({PostgreSQL})`).
Supports `ESCAPE` clause.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.code.similarTo("(SH\\|SZ)[0-9]{6}")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"code" SIMILAR TO ?         -- param: '(SH|SZ)[0-9]{6}'
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== notSimilarTo

PostgreSQL `NOT SIMILAR TO` (`@Support({PostgreSQL})`).

[source,java]
----
Stock_.name.notSimilarTo("%invalid%", SQLs.ESCAPE, "\\")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"name" NOT SIMILAR TO ? ESCAPE ?  -- params: '%invalid%', '\'
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== equalAny

`= ANY(...)` — true if equal to any row in the subquery.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.equalAny(subQuery)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" = ANY (SELECT ...)
----

===== equalSome

`= SOME(...)` — semantically identical to `equalAny`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.equalSome(subQuery)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" = SOME (SELECT ...)
----

===== equalAll

`= ALL(...)` — true if equal to every row in the subquery.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.equalAll(subQuery)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" = ALL (SELECT ...)
----

[source,java]

[source,sql]

===== in

`IN (...)` inclusion operator.
The right-hand side is a `SQLValueList`, typically provided via `SQLs.rowParam()` or a subquery.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.status.in(SQLs::rowParam, List.of(StockStatus.NORMAL, StockStatus.CLOSED))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"status" IN (?, ?)                -- params: NORMAL, CLOSED
----

[source,sql]

===== divide

`/` division.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.divide(new BigDecimal("2"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" / ?             -- param: 2
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

===== bitwiseAnd

`&` bitwise AND.
Returns a `BigInteger` typed expression.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.version.bitwiseAnd(0xFF)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"version" & ?      -- param: 255
----

[TIP]
====
The right-hand value is implicitly parameterized via `wrapRight` -> `SQLs.param(field, value)`
(DEFAULT mode), producing a JDBC `?` placeholder.
See <<parameter()>>, <<literalValue()>>, <<constValue()>> for explicit binding modes.
====

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)

===== rightShift

`>>` right bit shift.

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----

====

===== slice

Array slicing — accesses a slice of a PostgreSQL/H2 array (`@Support({H2, PostgreSQL})`).
Multiple overloads support 1D and 2D slicing; bounds can be expressions, literals, or `SQLs.ABSENT` (omitted bound).

[source,java]
----
// 1D slice: arr[lower:upper]
scores.slice(1, SQLs.COLON, 5)

// Omit lower: arr[:5]
scores.slice(SQLs.COLON, 5)

// Omit both ends: arr[:]
scores.slice(SQLs.COLON)

// 2D slice: arr[lower:upper][lower1:upper1]
matrix.slice(1, SQLs.COLON, 3, 1, SQLs.COLON, 3)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
scores[1:5]
scores[:5]
scores[:]
matrix[1:3][1:3]
----

===== sliceAtSubs

Array slicing via a `List` specifying nD slice bounds (`@Support({H2, PostgreSQL})`).

[source,java]
----
// nD slice: even-sized List of expression/literal/ABSENT elements
expr.sliceAtSubs(List.of(1, SQLs.COLON, 5, 1, SQLs.COLON, 3))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
expr[1:5][1:3]
----

===== dot

Dot operator — accesses fields of a composite type (Row Type), generating `(expr).fieldName` syntax.
Multiple overloads support 1–5 levels of nesting.

[source,java]
----
// Single-level access
compositeExpr.dot("field_name")

// Nested access
compositeExpr.dot("level1", "level2")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
(composite_expr)."field_name"
((composite_expr)."level1")."level2"
----

===== dots

Dot operator via a `List` for multi-level nesting.

[source,java]
----
expr.dots(List.of("a", "b", "c"))  // → (((expr)."a")."b")."c"
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
(((expr)."a")."b")."c"
----

===== bracket

Bracket operator — JSONB subscript access (`@Support({H2, PostgreSQL})`).
`bracket(key)` generates `['key']`.
Multiple overloads support 1–5 levels of nesting and `BiFunction` binding.

[source,java]
----
// Single-level JSONB access
jsonbExpr.bracket("name")

// Nested access
jsonbExpr.bracket("address", "city")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
jsonb_column['name']
jsonb_column['address']['city']
----

===== brackets

Bracket operator via a `List` for multi-level JSONB paths, supporting `BiFunction` binding.

[source,java]
----
expr.brackets(List.of("config", "timeout"))  // → ['config']['timeout']
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
expr['config']['timeout']
----

===== mapTo

Maps the expression to a known `MappingType` — does not change SQL output, only informs the Army type system of the target type.

[source,java]
----
SQLs.scalarSubQuery(subQuery).mapTo(IntegerType.INSTANCE)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Does not change SQL output; only affects Army's internal type inference
(SELECT count(*) FROM ...)
----

===== mapToArray

Maps the expression to an array type.

[source,java]
----
someExpr.mapToArray(ArrayMappingType.of(StringType.INSTANCE))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- Does not change SQL output
some_expr
----

===== castTo

SQL `CAST` — generates `CAST(expr AS type)` (`@Support({PostgreSQL})`).

[source,java]
----
Stock_.version.castTo(IntegerType.INSTANCE)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
CAST("version" AS INTEGER)
----

===== castToArray

SQL `CAST` to array — generates `CAST(expr AS type[])`.

[source,java]
----
someExpr.castToArray(ArrayMappingType.of(IntegerType.INSTANCE))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
CAST(some_expr AS INTEGER[])
----

===== asSortItem

Returns the expression itself as a `SortItem` (identity operation), for use in `ORDER BY`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.asSortItem()       // equivalent to asc() (default ascending)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" ASC
----

Ascending sort `ASC`.

Ascending + NULL ordering control.
Accepts `SQLs.NULLS_FIRST` / `SQLs.NULLS_LAST` or `null`.

[source,java]

----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"listing_date" ASC NULLS FIRST
----

Descending + NULL ordering control.

[source,java]

----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" DESC NULLS LAST
----

===== space

Dialect operator entry point — allows calling dual and binary operators beyond standard SQL.
The three-parameter overload supports modifiers.

[source,java]
----
// DualOperator overload — returns Expression
expr.space(someDualOperator, rightExpr)

// BiOperator overload — returns IPredicate
expr.space(someBiOperator, rightExpr)

// With modifier overload
expr.space(someBiOperator, rightExpr, modifier, optionalExpr)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
-- SQL output depends on the dialect operator definition; shown here for illustration only
expr <dialect_op> right_expr
expr <dialect_op> right_expr
expr <dialect_op> right_expr MODIFIER optional_expr
----

==== TypedExpression

[source,java]
----
public interface TypedExpression extends Expression, TypeInfer {
----

`TypedExpression` extends link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/Expression.java[`Expression`,role="extern"]
AND link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/TypeInfer.java[`TypeInfer`,role="extern"] — it carries a known `MappingType`, which enables Army to infer the SQL type of the right operand without value-class auto-detection.

Every metamodel field (e.g. `Stock_.name`) and every predicate (`IPredicate`) is a `TypedExpression` in practice.

[TIP]
====
Every method below takes `BiFunction<TypedExpression, T, Expression>` as its first parameter — a method reference to one of:

- `SQLs::param` — JDBC `?` placeholder (safe default)
- `SQLs::literal` — embeds value in SQL with type annotation (e.g. `DATE '...'`)
- `SQLs::constant` — embeds value without type prefix
- `SQLs::namedParam`, `SQLs::namedLiteral`, `SQLs::namedConst` — named variants for batch DML

See <<Parameter Binding>> and <<Literal Binding>> for full details.
====

===== equal

`=` operator with explicit binding control — always produces the chosen binding regardless of the global `LiteralMode`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.name.equal(SQLs::param, "ABC")
Stock_.regionType.equal(SQLs::literal, RegionType.PROVINCE)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"name" = ?              -- param: 'ABC'
"region_type" = 1        -- literal: PROVINCE (enum ordinal)
----

===== notEqual

`<>` operator with explicit binding.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.code.notEqual(SQLs::param, "000001")
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"code" <> ?              -- param: '000001'
----

===== nullSafeEqual

`IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` with explicit binding — the **only** safe way to pass `null`.
`Expression.nullSafeEqual(null)` throws because the single-arg `Object` overload cannot infer the type of a bare `null`.
`TypedExpression.nullSafeEqual(SQLs::param, null)` works because Army knows the
`MappingType` from the left operand.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.nullSafeEqual(SQLs::param, null)
Stock_.offerPrice.nullSafeEqual(SQLs::param, new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" IS NOT DISTINCT FROM ?      -- param: null
"offer_price" IS NOT DISTINCT FROM ?      -- param: 100.00
----

===== less

`<` operator with explicit binding.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.less(SQLs::param, new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" < ?        -- param: 100.00
----

===== lessEqual

`<=` operator with explicit binding.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.version.lessEqual(SQLs::param, 10)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"version" <= ?           -- param: 10
----

===== greater

`>` operator with explicit binding.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.greater(SQLs::param, new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" > ?        -- param: 100.00
----

===== greaterEqual

`>=` operator with explicit binding.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.listingDate.greaterEqual(SQLs::param, LocalDate.of(2024, 1, 1))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"listing_date" >= ?      -- param: 2024-01-01
----

===== between

`BETWEEN ... AND ...` with **per-bound binding control**.
Four overloads:

1. Single `BiFunction` for both bounds.
2. Independent `BiFunction` per bound — mix param and literal.
3-4. Same as above plus `SQLs.SYMMETRIC` / `SQLs.ASYMMETRIC` modifier (`@Support({PostgreSQL, H2})`).

[source,java]
----
// Single binding for both
Stock_.offerPrice.between(SQLs::param,
        new BigDecimal("10.00"), SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("100.00"))

// Different binding per bound
Stock_.offerPrice.between(SQLs::literal, new BigDecimal("10.00"),
        SQLs.AND, SQLs::param, new BigDecimal("100.00"))

// With SYMMETRIC modifier (PostgreSQL/H2)
Stock_.offerPrice.between(SQLs.SYMMETRIC, SQLs::param,
        new BigDecimal("100.00"), SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("10.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" BETWEEN ? AND ?              -- params: 10.00, 100.00
"offer_price" BETWEEN 10.00 AND ?           -- literal: 10.00 | param: 100.00
"offer_price" BETWEEN SYMMETRIC ? AND ?     -- params: 100.00, 10.00 (auto-swapped)
----

===== notBetween

`NOT BETWEEN ... AND ...` — same four overloads as `between`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.notBetween(SQLs::param,
        new BigDecimal("200.00"), SQLs.AND, new BigDecimal("500.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" NOT BETWEEN ? AND ?          -- params: 200.00, 500.00
----

===== is

`IS` with an `SQLs.IsComparisonWord` (e.g. `SQLs.DISTINCT_FROM`) and explicit binding (`@Support({PostgreSQL, H2})`).

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.is(SQLs.DISTINCT_FROM, SQLs::param, null)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" IS DISTINCT FROM ?           -- param: null
----

===== isNot

`IS NOT` with an `SQLs.IsComparisonWord` (`@Support({PostgreSQL, H2})`).

[source,java]
----
Stock_.offerPrice.isNot(SQLs.DISTINCT_FROM, SQLs::param, new BigDecimal("100.00"))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"offer_price" IS NOT DISTINCT FROM ?       -- param: 100.00
----

===== in

`IN (...)` with explicit binding.
Two overloads:

1. Collection-based — `BiFunction` converts the collection to a `RowExpression`.
2. Named-params — `TeNamedParamsFunc` for batch DML with a fixed parameter count.

[source,java]
----
// Collection binding
Stock_.status.in(SQLs::param, List.of(StockStatus.NORMAL, StockStatus.SUSPENDED))
Stock_.status.in(SQLs::literal, List.of(StockStatus.NORMAL, StockStatus.SUSPENDED))

// Named params for batch (size = 2)
Stock_.status.in(SQLs::namedParam, "statusList", 2)
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"status" IN (?, ?)          -- params: NORMAL, SUSPENDED
"status" IN (0, 1)           -- literals: enum ordinals
"status" IN (:statusList)    -- named: statusList (batch)
----

===== notIn

`NOT IN (...)` — same two overloads as `in`.

[source,java]
----
Stock_.status.notIn(SQLs::param, List.of(StockStatus.DELISTED))
----

.Generated SQL (PostgreSQL)
[source,sql]
----
"status" NOT IN (?)          -- param: DELISTED
----

===== space

Dialect operator entry point — three overloads:

1. `space(DualOperator, funcRef, value)` — returns `Expression`.
2. `space(BiOperator, funcRef, value)` — returns `IPredicate`.
3. `space(BiOperator, funcRef, value, modifier, optionalExp)` — with modifier.

[source,java]
----
expr.space(someDialectDualOp, SQLs::param, rightValue)
expr.space(someDialectBiOp, SQLs::param, rightValue)
expr.space(someDialectBiOp, SQLs::param, rightValue, SQLs.ESCAPE, '\\')
----

==== TypedField

[source,java]
----
public interface TypedField extends SqlField, TypedExpression, SimpleExpression {
----

`TypedField` is the base interface for all typed fields — it inherits from
`SqlField` (carries a field name), `TypedExpression` (carries a `MappingType`), and `SimpleExpression`.

Its two main implementation families:

- link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/TableField.java[`TableField`,role="extern"] — metamodel fields bound to real table columns (e.g. `Stock_.name`, `Stock_.price`)
- link:../army-core/src/main/java/io/army/criteria/TypedDerivedField.java[`TypedDerivedField`,role="extern"] — derived fields from subqueries, expressions, functions

===== Why `space` prefix
